Section 1:
A-Engrossed
House Bill 3991
Ordered by the House August 31
Including House Amendments dated August 31
Sponsored by JOINT SPECIAL SESSION COMMITTEE ON TRANSPORTATION FUNDING
SUMMARY
The following summary is not prepared by the sponsors of the measure and is not a part of the body thereof subject
to consideration by the Legislative Assembly. It is an editor’s brief statement of the essential features of the
measure. The statement includes a measure digest written in compliance with applicable readability standards.
Digest: The Act increases and adds taxes related to roads, cars, trucks and buses and says how
revenue must be used. The Act would make the per-mile road usage charge mandatory over time.
The Act would let a person pay a yearly fee instead of the per-mile road usage charge. The Act tells
the Division of Audits to do performance audits of ODOT. (Flesch Readability Score: 71.0).
Directs the Division of Audits to conduct performance audits of the Department of Transporta-
tion. Alters the duties of the Joint Committee on Transportation and the Continuous Improvement
Advisory Committee. Provides that the Governor shall appoint the Director of Transportation.
Increases and adds transportation-related fees and taxes. Provides uses of revenues.
Imposes a mandatory per-mile road usage charge for electric and hybrid vehicles. Allows an
annual fee in lieu of the mandatory per-mile road usage charge.
Repeals the mandatory toll program.
Provides for diesel fuel to be taxed in the same manner as gasoline.
Revises the formula for weight-mile taxes.
Takes effect on the 91st day following adjournment sine die.

2 SECTION 2. ORS 184.620 is amended to read:
3 184.620. (1) The Department of Transportation shall be under the supervision of a Director of
4 Transportation who shall be appointed by and shall hold office at the pleasure of the
5 Governor. [The Oregon Transportation Commission shall appoint the director, after consultation with
6 the Governor. The director serves at the pleasure of the commission.]
7 (2) The appointment of the director shall be subject to confirmation by the Senate in the manner
8 provided in ORS 184.623.
9 (3) The director may appoint:
10 (a) Deputy directors with full authority to act for the director, but subject to the director’s
11 control. The appointment of a deputy director shall be by written order filed with the Secretary of
12 State. A deputy director shall be in the unclassified services for purposes of the State Personnel
13 Relations Law.
14 (b) All subordinate officers and employees of the department and may prescribe their duties,
15 assignments and reassignments and fix their compensation, subject to any applicable provisions of
16 the State Personnel Relations Law.
17 (4) Subject to the approval of the [commission] Oregon Transportation Commission, the di-
18 rector may organize and reorganize the department as the director considers necessary to properly
19 conduct the work of the department. As directed by the chairperson of the commission, the director
20 shall assign employees of the department to staff the commission.
21 (5) When service of summons or other process is required by statute to be served on the Di-
22 rector of Transportation, the Department of Transportation or the Oregon Transportation Commis-
23 sion, such service shall be made upon the office of the director.
24 SECTION 3. ORS 184.623 is amended to read:
25 184.623. (1) The executive appointment of the Director of Transportation by the [Oregon Trans-
26 portation Commission] Governor under ORS 184.620 is subject to confirmation by the Senate. Con-
27 firmation requires the affirmative vote of a majority of the members of the Senate.
28 (2) If an appointment made under ORS 184.620 is not confirmed by the Senate, the [commission]
29 Governor shall make another appointment, subject to confirmation by the Senate.
30 (3) The name of the individual to be appointed or reappointed shall be submitted to the Senate
31 by the [commission] Governor under ORS 184.620. The Senate shall take up the question of confir-
32 mation as soon after the convening of a regular or special session as is appropriate. The question
33 of confirmation may be referred to committee or may be acted upon without a referral.
34 (4) If the name of an individual to be appointed or reappointed submitted by the [commission]
35 Governor is not acted upon during the term of the Legislative Assembly to which it is submitted,
36 the name may be resubmitted to the subsequent term by the [commission] Governor on or after the
37 date the Legislative Assembly convenes in the subsequent regular session.
38 SECTION 4. (1) The amendments to ORS 184.620 and 184.623 by sections 2 and 3 of this
39 2025 special session Act apply to appointments made on or after the effective date of this 2025
40 special session Act.
41 (2) The Director of Transportation who is serving on the effective date of this 2025 special
42 session Act continues to be governed by ORS 184.620 as in effect immediately before the ef-
43 fective date of this 2025 special session Act.

1 SECTION 7. ORS 171.861 is amended to read:
2 171.861. (1) As used in this section, “major project” means a transportation project that
3 costs $250 million or more to complete.
4 (2) The Joint Committee on Transportation shall:
5 (a) Examine transportation related policy [and];
6 (b) Review transportation project expenditures;
7 (c) Review the scope, schedule, changes and budget updates to major projects on a
8 quarterly basis;
9 (d) Review requests for project scope expansion submitted by a city or a county under
10 section 8 of this 2025 special session Act; and
11 (e) Make recommendations related to transportation and appropriation of funding to the Joint
12 Committee on Ways and Means during the period when the Legislative Assembly is in session,
13 or to the Emergency Board or the Joint Interim Committee on Ways and Means during the
14 interim period between sessions.
15 (3) The Joint Committee on Transportation shall provide general legislative oversight of the
16 Department of Transportation and the Oregon Department of Aviation.
17 SECTION 8. (1) As used in this section, “highway improvement project” means a state
18 highway project for which the Department of Transportation may use federal transportation
19 funds.
20 (2) If a city or county proposes to expand the scope of a highway improvement project,
21 but does not provide funding, the city or county shall submit the proposed change to the
22 Oregon Transportation Commission. If the commission approves the proposed change, the
23 commission shall submit a report to the Joint Committee on Transportation that informs the
24 committee about the proposed change and cost associated with the expanded scope. After
25 reviewing the report, the committee may submit recommendations for appropriations that
26 may be made in the future to cover the costs of the expanded scope of the highway im-
27 provement project.
28 (3) This section applies to highway improvement projects when a city or county is not
29 covering the costs of the expanded scope and:
30 (a) The project costs less than $25 million and the changes in scope the city or county
31 is requesting increase the project costs by 10 percent or more; or
32 (b) The project costs $25 million or more and the changes in scope the city or county is
33 requesting increase the project costs by five percent or more.
34 SECTION 9. The Legislative Policy and Research Director shall enter into a professional
35 services contract for a performance audit of the operations of the Department of Transpor-
36 tation, to include examination of:
37 (1) The management of the department; and
38 (2) Whether and how the department addresses recommendations from the management

40 5550).

42 SECTION 11. ORS 366.506 is amended to read:
43 366.506. (1) Once every two years, the Oregon Department of Administrative Services shall
44 conduct a highway cost allocation study. The purpose of the study is to determine:
45 (a) The proportionate share that the users of each class of vehicle should pay for the costs of
[4]
A-Eng. HB 3991
1 maintenance, operation and improvement of the highways, roads and streets in the state; and
2 (b) Whether the users of each class are paying that share.
3 (2) Each study must include:
4 (a) An examination of the most recent study period for which actual data are available for the
5 purpose of determining the accuracy of the most recently published study results; and
6 (b) An examination of the prospective study period based on projected data for the purpose de-
7 scribed in subsection (1) of this section that incorporates the results of the examination de-
8 scribed in paragraph (a) of this subsection.
9 (3) The department may use any study design the department determines will best accomplish
10 the purposes stated in subsection (1) of this section. In designing the study, the department may
11 make decisions that include, but are not limited to, the methodology to be used for the study, what
12 constitutes a class of vehicle for purposes of collection of data under subsections (1) to (5) of this
13 section and the nature and scope of costs that will be included in the study.
14 (4) The department may appoint a study review team to participate in the study required by
15 subsection (1) of this section. The team may perform any functions assigned by the department, in-
16 cluding, but not limited to, consulting on the design of the study.
17 (5) A report on the results of the study shall be submitted to the legislative revenue committees
18 and the Joint Committee on Transportation by January 31 of each odd-numbered year.
19 (6) The Legislative Assembly shall use the report described in subsection (5) of this section to
20 determine whether adjustments to revenue sources described in Article IX, section 3a (3), of the
21 Oregon Constitution, are needed in order to carry out the purposes of Article IX, section 3a (3), of
22 the Oregon Constitution. If such adjustments are needed, the Legislative Assembly shall enact
23 whatever measures are necessary to make the adjustments.

22 SECTION 13. The amendments to ORS 366.506 by section 12 of this 2025 special session
23 Act become operative on January 1, 2030.
24 SECTION 14. (1) In consultation with the study review team described in ORS 366.506,
25 the Oregon Department of Administrative Services shall undertake a review of the method-
26 ology for the highway cost allocation study required under ORS 366.506.
27 (2) The department shall examine all aspects of the methodology for the highway cost
28 allocation study, including but not limited to the following:
29 (a) The revenues and expenditures included in the highway cost allocation study;
30 (b) How costs are allocated across different classes of vehicles;
31 (c) What constitutes a class of vehicle;
32 (d) The data used in the highway cost allocation study;
33 (e) The level of granularity to which cost responsibility is calculated for potential rate
34 changes; and
35 (f) Whether equity should be analyzed based on an estimate of the future biennium’s re-
36 venue and expenditures or a retrospective analysis of past actual revenue and expenditures.
37 (3) The department may provide recommendations for updating the methodology for the
38 study, including any changes in statute needed to improve the outcome of the study and
39 ensure fairness and proportionate revenue and costs for each class of vehicle.
40 (4) The department shall submit a report in the manner provided by ORS 192.245, and
41 may include recommendations for legislation, to the Joint Committee on Transportation no
42 later than June 30, 2026.
43 SECTION 15. Section 14 of this 2025 special session Act is repealed on January 2, 2027.

1 SECTION 16. ORS 319.020 is amended to read:
2 319.020. (1) Subject to subsections (2) to (4) of this section, in addition to the taxes otherwise
3 provided for by law, every dealer engaging in the dealer’s own name, or in the name of others, in
4 the first sale, use or distribution of motor vehicle fuel or aircraft fuel or withdrawal of motor vehicle
5 fuel or aircraft fuel for sale, use or distribution within areas in this state within which the state
6 lacks the power to tax the sale, use or distribution of motor vehicle fuel or aircraft fuel, shall:
7 (a) Not later than the 25th day of each calendar month, render a statement to the Department
8 of Transportation of all motor vehicle fuel or aircraft fuel sold, used, distributed or so withdrawn
9 by the dealer in the State of Oregon as well as all such fuel sold, used or distributed in this state
10 by a purchaser thereof upon which sale, use or distribution the dealer has assumed liability for the
11 applicable license tax during the preceding calendar month. The dealer shall render the statement
12 to the department in the manner provided by the department by rule.
13 (b) Except as provided in ORS 319.270, pay a license tax computed on the basis of [34] 46 cents
14 per gallon on the first sale, use or distribution of such motor vehicle fuel or aircraft fuel so sold,
15 used, distributed or withdrawn as shown by such statement in the manner and within the time pro-
16 vided in ORS 319.010 to 319.430.
17 (2) When aircraft fuel is sold, used or distributed by a dealer, the license tax shall be computed
18 on the basis of 11 cents per gallon of fuel so sold, used or distributed, except that when aircraft fuel
19 usable in aircraft operated by turbine engines (turbo-prop or jet) is sold, used or distributed, the tax
20 rate shall be three cents per gallon.
21 (3) In lieu of claiming refund of the tax paid on motor vehicle fuel consumed by such dealer in
22 nonhighway use as provided in ORS 319.280, 319.290 and 319.320, or of any prior erroneous payment
23 of license tax made to the state by such dealer, the dealer may show such motor vehicle fuel as a
24 credit or deduction on the monthly statement and payment of tax.
25 (4) The license tax computed on the basis of the sale, use, distribution or withdrawal of motor
26 vehicle or aircraft fuel may not be imposed wherever such tax is prohibited by the Constitution or
27 laws of the United States with respect to such tax.
28 SECTION 17. ORS 319.530 is amended to read:
29 319.530. (1) To compensate this state partially for the use of its highways, an excise tax hereby
30 is imposed at the rate of [34] 46 cents per gallon on the use of fuel in a motor vehicle.
31 (2) Except as otherwise provided in subsections (3) to (6) of this section, 100 cubic feet of fuel
32 used or sold in a gaseous state, measured at 14.73 pounds per square inch of pressure at 60 degrees
33 Fahrenheit, is taxable at the same rate as a gallon of liquid fuel.
34 (3) 123.57 cubic feet, or 5.66 pounds, of compressed natural gas used or sold in a gaseous state
35 is taxable at the same rate as one gasoline gallon.
36 (4) 1.353 gallons, or 5.75 pounds, of liquefied petroleum gas is taxable at the same rate as one
37 gasoline gallon.
38 (5) 1.71 gallons, or 6.059 pounds, of liquefied natural gas is taxable at the same rate as one diesel
39 gallon.
40 (6) One kilogram of hydrogen is taxable at the same rate as one gasoline gallon.

12 SECTION 24. ORS 320.550 is amended to read:
13 320.550. (1) As used in this section:
14 (a) “Employer” has the meaning given that term in ORS 316.162.
15 (b) “Resident of this state” has the meaning given that term in ORS 316.027.
16 (c) “Wages” has the meaning given that term in ORS 316.162.
17 (2) A tax is imposed at the rate of [one-tenth] two-tenths of one percent of the wages of an
18 employee who is:
19 (a) A resident of this state, regardless of where services are performed.
20 (b) Not a resident of this state, for services performed in this state.
21 (3) Every employer at the time of the payment of wages shall deduct and withhold from the total
22 amount of the wages paid for services described under subsection (2) of this section an amount equal
23 to the total amount of wages multiplied by the rate of tax imposed under subsection (2) of this sec-
24 tion.
25 (4) An employer shall report and pay the tax imposed under this section to the Department of
26 Revenue at the time and in the manner determined by the department by rule.
27 (5) For purposes of the tax imposed under this section, an employer is considered a taxpayer.
28 (6) If a lender, surety or other person who supplies funds to or for the account of an employer
29 for the purpose of paying wages of the employees of such employer has actual notice or knowledge
30 that such employer does not intend to or will not be able to make timely payment or deposit of the
31 tax required to be deducted and withheld, such lender, surety or other person shall be liable to the
32 State of Oregon in a sum equal to the taxes, together with interest, that are not timely paid over
33 to the Department of Revenue. Such liability shall be limited to the principal amount supplied by
34 the lender, surety or other person, and any amounts so paid to the department shall be credited
35 against the liability of the employer.
36 (7)(a) An employer shall submit an annual return pursuant to ORS 316.202 to the Department
37 of Revenue. The amounts deducted from the wages during any calendar year in accordance with this
38 section shall be considered to be in payment of the tax imposed under subsection (2) of this section.
39 (b) The return submitted by the employer shall be accepted by the Department of Revenue as
40 evidence in favor of the employee of the amounts so deducted from the employee’s wages.
41 (8) Nothing in this section prohibits the Department of Revenue from including the tax imposed
42 under this section in the combined quarterly tax report required under ORS 316.168.
43 (9) An employer that fails to deduct and withhold the tax required under this section:
44 (a) Is deemed responsible for the payment of the tax obligation in an amount equal to the
45 amount required to be withheld from the employee’s wages and remitted to the Department of Re-
[17]
A-Eng. HB 3991
1 venue; and
2 (b) Is subject to a penalty of $250 per employee, up to a maximum penalty of $25,000, if the
3 employer knowingly fails to deduct and withhold the tax.
4 (10) Residents subject to the tax imposed under this section on wages earned outside this state
5 from an employer not doing business within this state shall report and pay the tax in an amount
6 not to exceed [one-tenth] two-tenths of one percent of the wages earned outside this state, and at
7 the time and in the manner, as determined by the Department of Revenue by rule.

30 authorized by this section, the department may:

34 to and use of amounts in those subaccounts; and

36 trust funds or accounts all or any portion of the amounts that are required to be deposited in the

39 pledge any funds or amounts at any time held in the Toll Program Fund as security for the obli-
40 gations of a unit of government or a private entity unless the department has entered into a binding
41 and enforceable agreement that provides the department reasonable assurance that the department
42 will be repaid, with appropriate interest, any amounts that the department is required to advance
43 pursuant to that pledge.

45 poses authorized by this section.

A-Eng. HB 3991

13 SECTION 64. Sections 65 to 67 of this 2025 special session Act are added to and made a
14 part of the Oregon Vehicle Code.
15 SECTION 65. “Dyed diesel” has the meaning given that term in ORS 319.520.
16 SECTION 66. (1) A person commits the offense of failure to comply with an international
17 fuel tax agreement if the person is required to comply with the requirements of an interna-
18 tional fuel tax agreement entered into under ORS 825.555 or any rule adopted by the De-
19 partment of Transportation under ORS 825.555, and the person fails to comply.
20 (2) The offense described under this section, failure to comply with an international fuel
21 tax agreement, is a Class A traffic violation.
22 SECTION 67. (1) A person commits the offense of improper use of dyed diesel if the
23 person operates a motor vehicle on the highways of this state and has dyed diesel in the fuel
24 supply tank of the vehicle in violation of section 71 of this 2025 special session Act.
25 (2) The offense described under this section, improper use of dyed diesel, is a Class A
26 traffic violation.

41 319.600, if, for all fuel used in a motor vehicle in this state, the nonresident pays to a seller, at the
42 time of the sale, the tax provided in ORS 319.530.
43 (3) A user’s license is not required for a person who uses fuel in a motor vehicle if, for all fuel
44 used in a motor vehicle in this state, the person pays to a seller, at the time of the sale, the tax
45 provided in ORS 319.530.

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 (4) A user’s license is not required for a person who is subject to the weight-mile tax described

15 SECTION 70. Sections 71 and 72 of this 2025 special session Act are added to and made
16 a part of ORS 319.510 to 319.880.
17 SECTION 71. Dyed diesel use. (1) A person may operate or maintain a motor vehicle on
18 the highways of this state with dyed diesel in the fuel supply tank only if the use is author-
19 ized by an agency of the United States or the person is eligible for a refund under ORS
20 267.570 (2) or 319.831.
21 (2) A person that owns, operates or maintains a fuel storage tank or terminal storage
22 facility:
23 (a) Shall provide markings consistent with those directed by federal law; and
24 (b) May not knowingly store, or cause to be stored, dyed diesel in a fuel storage tank or
25 terminal storage facility if the purpose of the tank or facility is to store undyed diesel.
26 (3) A person that violates this section is subject to a civil penalty under section 72 of this
27 2025 special session Act.
28 SECTION 72. Civil penalties. (1) In addition to any other penalty provided by law, the
29 Department of Transportation may impose a civil penalty for failure to comply with section
30 71 of this 2025 special session Act.
31 (2) Any civil penalty imposed under this section shall be imposed in the manner provided
32 by ORS 183.745.
33 (3) The department shall adopt rules implementing these provisions, including a schedule
34 of civil penalties.
35 (4) The civil penalty for each violation of section 71 of this 2025 special session Act may
36 not exceed the amount of $10 per gallon of capacity of the fuel supply tank of the motor ve-
37 hicle, or $1,000, whichever is greater, plus the amount of tax that would have been paid for
38 an equivalent amount of motor vehicle fuel.
39 (5) A civil penalty imposed under this section may be remitted or reduced upon such
40 terms and conditions as the department considers proper and consistent with the public
41 health and safety.
42 (6)(a) In imposing a penalty pursuant to the schedule adopted pursuant to this section,
43 the department shall consider the following factors:
44 (A) Any prior violations of section 71 of this 2025 special session Act.
45 (B) The extent to which the violation threatens the public health or safety and the
[40]
A-Eng. HB 3991
1 immediacy of the threat.
2 (b) The penalty imposed under this section may be remitted or mitigated upon such
3 terms and conditions as the department determines to be proper and consistent with the
4 public benefit.
5 (7) All penalties recovered under this section shall be paid into the State Treasury and
6 credited to the State Highway Fund.
7 SECTION 73. ORS 319.700 is amended to read:
8 319.700. The tax and the penalty imposed upon a user of fuel in a motor vehicle by ORS 319.510
9 to 319.880 or penalties associated with the improper use or storage of dyed diesel under
10 sections 71 and 72 of this 2025 special session Act shall constitute a lien upon, and shall have
11 the effect of an execution duly levied against, any motor vehicle in connection with which the tax-
12 able use is made, attaching at the time of such use. The lien shall not be removed until the tax has
13 been paid or the motor vehicle subject to the lien has been sold in payment of such tax. The lien

15 to the rights of any conditional vendor or any other holder of the legal title in or to the motor ve-
16 hicle.

13 SECTION 79. Section 80 of this 2025 special session Act is added to and made a part of
14 ORS chapter 825.
15 SECTION 80. (1) Before operating a motor vehicle on the public highways of this state,
16 an out-of-state motor carrier not licensed under an international fuel tax agreement shall
17 obtain a valid fuel trip permit from the Department of Transportation in accordance with
18 this section. A motor carrier shall obtain a fuel trip permit under this section if:
19 (a) The motor carrier is operating a motor vehicle that is not a recreational vehicle:
20 (A) Having two axles and a gross vehicle weight or registered gross vehicle weight ex-
21 ceeding 26,000 pounds;
22 (B) Having three or more axles regardless of weight; or
23 (C) Used in combination, when the weight of such combination exceeds 26,000 pounds; and
24 (b) The vehicle is not registered under ORS 826.009 or 826.031.
25 (2) Subsection (1) of this section does not apply to a motor carrier that has a valid
26 international fuel tax agreement license issued by a jurisdiction other than Oregon.
27 (3) The Department of Transportation shall develop a standardized application form for
28 a fuel trip permit issued under this section.
29 (4) The department may not issue more than three fuel trip permits in a calendar year
30 for any one motor vehicle.
31 (5) No report of mileage is required for the motor vehicle to which the fuel trip permit
32 relates.
33 (6) A fuel trip permit issued under this section is valid:
34 (a) For three consecutive days beginning and ending on the dates specified on the face
35 of the fuel trip permit; and
36 (b) Only for the motor vehicle for which the fuel trip permit was issued.
37 (7) The fee for the fuel trip permit shall be determined by the department by rule.
38 (8) The department may adopt rules to carry out the provisions of this section.

15 SECTION 94. ORS 825.474 is amended to read:
16 825.474. (1) In addition to other fees and taxes imposed by law upon carriers, there shall be as-
17 sessed against and collected from every carrier a tax for the use of the highways, to apply to the
18 cost of administration of this chapter and for the maintenance, operation, construction and recon-
19 struction of public highways.
20 (2) The tax rate which shall apply to each motor vehicle shall be based upon the declared
21 combined weight of the motor vehicle and in accordance with the weight group tax rates as shown
22 in the tables set forth in ORS 825.476.
23 (3) For the purpose of computing the tax due:
24 (a) Table “A” in ORS 825.476 applies to motor vehicles subject to the tax imposed by this sec-
25 tion [that are not issued an annual variance permit under ORS 818.200 (1)(a) to (c) to operate with a
26 combined weight of more than 80,000 pounds].
27 [(b) Table “B” applies to motor vehicles subject to the tax imposed by this section that are issued
28 or required to obtain an annual variance permit under ORS 818.200 (1)(a) to (c) to operate with a
29 combined weight of more than 80,000 pounds.]
30 [(c)] (b) The declared combined weight shall be the combined weight, as defined in ORS 825.005,
31 declared in the [application for authority under ORS 825.100, subject to audit and approval by the
32 Department of Transportation] registration weight.
33 [(d)] (c) In addition to any tax due under this chapter, motor vehicles that exceed the maximum
34 vehicle weight limits for annual variance permits under ORS 818.200 (1)(a) to (c) are subject to the
35 road use assessment fee imposed under ORS 818.225 for the entire motor vehicle weight, minus the
36 road use assessment fee for the maximum vehicle weight allowed under the annual variance permit.
37 (4) The tax for each motor vehicle [when table “A” or “B” is used] shall be computed by multi-
38 plying the extreme mileage of travel in Oregon by the appropriate weight group tax rate as it ap-
39 pears in the table.

2 SECTION 98. ORS 818.225 is amended to read:
3 818.225. (1) As used in this section, “equivalent single-axle load” means the relationship between
4 actual or requested weight and an 18,000 pound single-axle load as determined by the American
5 Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials Road Tests reported at the Proceedings
6 Conference of 1962.
7 (2)(a) In addition to any fee for a single-trip nondivisible load permit, a person who is issued the
8 permit or who operates a vehicle in a manner that requires the permit is liable for payment of a
9 road use assessment fee of [ten and nine-tenths] seven and nine-tenths cents per equivalent
10 single-axle load mile traveled.
11 (b) If the road use assessment fee is not collected at the time of issuance of the permit, the de-
12 partment shall bill the permittee for the amount due. The account shall be considered delinquent if
13 not paid within 60 days of billing.
14 (c) The miles of travel authorized by a single-trip nondivisible load permit shall be exempt from
15 taxation under ORS chapter 825.
16 (3) The department may adopt rules:
17 (a) To standardize the determination of equivalent single-axle load computation based on aver-
18 age highway conditions; and
19 (b) To establish procedures for payment, collection and enforcement of the fees and assessments
20 established by this chapter.

24 98 of this 2025 special session Act become operative on July 1, 2029.

28 98 of this 2025 special session Act apply to taxes imposed on or after July 1, 2029.

Raw Text:
83rd OREGON LEGISLATIVE ASSEMBLY--2025 Special Session
A-Engrossed
House Bill 3991
Ordered by the House August 31
Including House Amendments dated August 31
Sponsored by JOINT SPECIAL SESSION COMMITTEE ON TRANSPORTATION FUNDING
SUMMARY
The following summary is not prepared by the sponsors of the measure and is not a part of the body thereof subject
to consideration by the Legislative Assembly. It is an editor’s brief statement of the essential features of the
measure. The statement includes a measure digest written in compliance with applicable readability standards.
Digest: The Act increases and adds taxes related to roads, cars, trucks and buses and says how
revenue must be used. The Act would make the per-mile road usage charge mandatory over time.
The Act would let a person pay a yearly fee instead of the per-mile road usage charge. The Act tells
the Division of Audits to do performance audits of ODOT. (Flesch Readability Score: 71.0).
Directs the Division of Audits to conduct performance audits of the Department of Transporta-
tion. Alters the duties of the Joint Committee on Transportation and the Continuous Improvement
Advisory Committee. Provides that the Governor shall appoint the Director of Transportation.
Increases and adds transportation-related fees and taxes. Provides uses of revenues.
Imposes a mandatory per-mile road usage charge for electric and hybrid vehicles. Allows an
annual fee in lieu of the mandatory per-mile road usage charge.
Repeals the mandatory toll program.
Provides for diesel fuel to be taxed in the same manner as gasoline.
Revises the formula for weight-mile taxes.
Takes effect on the 91st day following adjournment sine die.

3 184.620. (1) The Department of Transportation shall be under the supervision of a Director of
4 Transportation who shall be appointed by and shall hold office at the pleasure of the
5 Governor. [The Oregon Transportation Commission shall appoint the director, after consultation with
6 the Governor. The director serves at the pleasure of the commission.]
7 (2) The appointment of the director shall be subject to confirmation by the Senate in the manner
8 provided in ORS 184.623.
9 (3) The director may appoint:
10 (a) Deputy directors with full authority to act for the director, but subject to the director’s
11 control. The appointment of a deputy director shall be by written order filed with the Secretary of
12 State. A deputy director shall be in the unclassified services for purposes of the State Personnel
13 Relations Law.
14 (b) All subordinate officers and employees of the department and may prescribe their duties,
15 assignments and reassignments and fix their compensation, subject to any applicable provisions of
16 the State Personnel Relations Law.

18 rector may organize and reorganize the department as the director considers necessary to properly
19 conduct the work of the department. As directed by the chairperson of the commission, the director
20 shall assign employees of the department to staff the commission.
21 (5) When service of summons or other process is required by statute to be served on the Di-
22 rector of Transportation, the Department of Transportation or the Oregon Transportation Commis-
23 sion, such service shall be made upon the office of the director.
24 SECTION 3. ORS 184.623 is amended to read:
25 184.623. (1) The executive appointment of the Director of Transportation by the [Oregon Trans-
26 portation Commission] Governor under ORS 184.620 is subject to confirmation by the Senate. Con-
27 firmation requires the affirmative vote of a majority of the members of the Senate.
28 (2) If an appointment made under ORS 184.620 is not confirmed by the Senate, the [commission]
29 Governor shall make another appointment, subject to confirmation by the Senate.
30 (3) The name of the individual to be appointed or reappointed shall be submitted to the Senate
31 by the [commission] Governor under ORS 184.620. The Senate shall take up the question of confir-
32 mation as soon after the convening of a regular or special session as is appropriate. The question
33 of confirmation may be referred to committee or may be acted upon without a referral.
34 (4) If the name of an individual to be appointed or reappointed submitted by the [commission]
35 Governor is not acted upon during the term of the Legislative Assembly to which it is submitted,
36 the name may be resubmitted to the subsequent term by the [commission] Governor on or after the
37 date the Legislative Assembly convenes in the subsequent regular session.

40 special session Act.
41 (2) The Director of Transportation who is serving on the effective date of this 2025 special
42 session Act continues to be governed by ORS 184.620 as in effect immediately before the ef-
43 fective date of this 2025 special session Act.

1 SECTION 7. ORS 171.861 is amended to read:
2 171.861. (1) As used in this section, “major project” means a transportation project that
3 costs $250 million or more to complete.
4 (2) The Joint Committee on Transportation shall:
5 (a) Examine transportation related policy [and];
6 (b) Review transportation project expenditures;
7 (c) Review the scope, schedule, changes and budget updates to major projects on a
8 quarterly basis;
9 (d) Review requests for project scope expansion submitted by a city or a county under
10 section 8 of this 2025 special session Act; and
11 (e) Make recommendations related to transportation and appropriation of funding to the Joint
12 Committee on Ways and Means during the period when the Legislative Assembly is in session,
13 or to the Emergency Board or the Joint Interim Committee on Ways and Means during the
14 interim period between sessions.
15 (3) The Joint Committee on Transportation shall provide general legislative oversight of the
16 Department of Transportation and the Oregon Department of Aviation.
17 SECTION 8. (1) As used in this section, “highway improvement project” means a state
18 highway project for which the Department of Transportation may use federal transportation
19 funds.
20 (2) If a city or county proposes to expand the scope of a highway improvement project,
21 but does not provide funding, the city or county shall submit the proposed change to the
22 Oregon Transportation Commission. If the commission approves the proposed change, the
23 commission shall submit a report to the Joint Committee on Transportation that informs the
24 committee about the proposed change and cost associated with the expanded scope. After
25 reviewing the report, the committee may submit recommendations for appropriations that
26 may be made in the future to cover the costs of the expanded scope of the highway im-
27 provement project.
28 (3) This section applies to highway improvement projects when a city or county is not
29 covering the costs of the expanded scope and:
30 (a) The project costs less than $25 million and the changes in scope the city or county
31 is requesting increase the project costs by 10 percent or more; or
32 (b) The project costs $25 million or more and the changes in scope the city or county is
33 requesting increase the project costs by five percent or more.
34 SECTION 9. The Legislative Policy and Research Director shall enter into a professional
35 services contract for a performance audit of the operations of the Department of Transpor-
36 tation, to include examination of:
37 (1) The management of the department; and
38 (2) Whether and how the department addresses recommendations from the management
39 review conducted pursuant to section 203, chapter 7, Oregon Laws 2025 (Enrolled Senate Bill
40 5550).
41 SECTION 10. Section 9 of this 2025 special session Act is repealed on January 2, 2027.

11 make decisions that include, but are not limited to, the methodology to be used for the study, what
12 constitutes a class of vehicle for purposes of collection of data under subsections (1) to (5) of this
13 section and the nature and scope of costs that will be included in the study.
14 (4) The department may appoint a study review team to participate in the study required by
15 subsection (1) of this section. The team may perform any functions assigned by the department, in-
16 cluding, but not limited to, consulting on the design of the study.
17 (5) A report on the results of the study shall be submitted to the legislative revenue committees
18 and the Joint Committee on Transportation by January 31 of each odd-numbered year.
19 (6) The Legislative Assembly shall use the report described in subsection (5) of this section to
20 determine whether adjustments to revenue sources described in Article IX, section 3a (3), of the
21 Oregon Constitution, are needed in order to carry out the purposes of Article IX, section 3a (3), of
22 the Oregon Constitution. If such adjustments are needed, the Legislative Assembly shall enact
23 whatever measures are necessary to make the adjustments.
24 SECTION 12. ORS 366.506, as amended by section 11 of this 2025 special session Act, is
25 amended to read:
26 366.506. (1) Once every two years, the Oregon Department of Administrative Services shall
27 conduct a highway cost allocation study. The purpose of the study is to determine:
28 (a) The proportionate share that the users of each class of vehicle should pay for the costs of
29 maintenance, operation and improvement of the highways, roads and streets in the state; and
30 (b) Whether the users of each class are paying that share.
31 (2) Each study must include:
32 (a) An examination of the most recent study period for which actual data are available for the
33 purpose of determining the accuracy of the most recently published study results; and
34 (b) An examination of the prospective study period based on projected data for the purpose de-
35 scribed in subsection (1) of this section that incorporates the results of the examination described
36 in paragraph (a) of this subsection.
37 (3) The department may use any study design the department determines will best accomplish
38 the purposes stated in subsection (1) of this section. In designing the study, the department may
39 make decisions that include, but are not limited to, the methodology to be used for the study, what
40 constitutes a class of vehicle for purposes of collection of data under subsections (1) to (5) of this
41 section and the nature and scope of costs that will be included in the study.
42 (4) The department may appoint a study review team to participate in the study required by
43 subsection (1) of this section. The team may perform any functions assigned by the department, in-
44 cluding, but not limited to, consulting on the design of the study.
45 (5) A report on the results of the study shall be submitted to the legislative revenue committees
[5]

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 and the Joint Committee on Transportation by January 31 of each odd-numbered year.
2 (6) The Legislative Assembly shall use the report described in subsection (5) of this section to
3 determine whether adjustments to revenue sources described in Article IX, section 3a (3), of the
4 Oregon Constitution, are needed in order to carry out the purposes of Article IX, section 3a (3), of
5 the Oregon Constitution. If such adjustments are needed, the Legislative Assembly shall enact
6 whatever measures are necessary to make the adjustments.
7 (7)(a) This subsection applies if:
8 (A) The highway cost allocation report indicates that the equity ratio for the heavy ve-
9 hicle class or the light vehicle class is at least 1.05; and
10 (B) The Legislative Assembly has not complied with subsection (6) of this section within
11 120 days following the date on which the Joint Committee on Transportation received the
12 report submitted under subsection (5) of this section.
13 (b)(A) On or after September 1 of each odd-numbered year, the department shall adopt
14 rules that lower the fee rates per mile set forth in ORS 825.476 or the fuel tax rates set forth
15 in ORS 319.020 (1)(b) and 319.530 (1) as necessary so that whichever class has an equity ratio
16 of 1.05 or greater will have an equity ratio of 1.045.
17 (B) Adjustments to the fuel tax rates shall be rounded to the nearest 0.1 cents per gallon.
18 (8) The department shall repeal any rule adopted pursuant to subsection (7) of this sec-
19 tion if the department determines that, after the rule was adopted, the Legislative Assembly
20 adjusted revenue sources to carry out the purposes of Article IX, section 3a (3), of the
21 Oregon Constitution.
22 SECTION 13. The amendments to ORS 366.506 by section 12 of this 2025 special session
23 Act become operative on January 1, 2030.
24 SECTION 14. (1) In consultation with the study review team described in ORS 366.506,
25 the Oregon Department of Administrative Services shall undertake a review of the method-
26 ology for the highway cost allocation study required under ORS 366.506.
27 (2) The department shall examine all aspects of the methodology for the highway cost
28 allocation study, including but not limited to the following:
29 (a) The revenues and expenditures included in the highway cost allocation study;
30 (b) How costs are allocated across different classes of vehicles;
31 (c) What constitutes a class of vehicle;
32 (d) The data used in the highway cost allocation study;
33 (e) The level of granularity to which cost responsibility is calculated for potential rate
34 changes; and
35 (f) Whether equity should be analyzed based on an estimate of the future biennium’s re-
36 venue and expenditures or a retrospective analysis of past actual revenue and expenditures.
37 (3) The department may provide recommendations for updating the methodology for the
38 study, including any changes in statute needed to improve the outcome of the study and
39 ensure fairness and proportionate revenue and costs for each class of vehicle.
40 (4) The department shall submit a report in the manner provided by ORS 192.245, and
41 may include recommendations for legislation, to the Joint Committee on Transportation no
42 later than June 30, 2026.
43 SECTION 15. Section 14 of this 2025 special session Act is repealed on January 2, 2027.

15 to the following:
16 (a) The moneys shall be distributed to all the cities.
17 (b) Each city shall receive such share of the moneys as its population bears to the total popu-
18 lation of the cities.
19 (2) Each year, the sum of [$2,500,000] $3,000,000 shall be withdrawn from the appropriation
20 specified in ORS 366.800 and [$2,500,000] $3,000,000 shall be withdrawn from moneys available to the
21 Department of Transportation from the State Highway Fund. The sums withdrawn shall be trans-
22 ferred to a separate account to be administered by the Department of Transportation. The following
23 apply to the account described in this subsection:
24 (a) Money from the account shall be used only on roads:
25 (A) That are not a part of the state highway system, with the exception of project elements that
26 are required to comply with federal or state law;
27 (B) That are within, or under the jurisdiction of, cities with populations of 5,000 or fewer
28 persons; and
29 (C) That are inadequate for the capacity the roads serve or are in a condition detrimental to
30 safety.
31 (b) To the extent moneys are available to fund whole projects, all moneys in the account shall
32 be allocated each year.
33 (c) Subject to paragraph (d) of this subsection, the department shall determine annual allocation
34 after considering applications, including project budgets, submitted by the cities to the department.
35 (d) The department may enter into agreements with cities upon the advice and counsel of the
36 small city advisory committee to determine allocation based on those applications.
37 (3) The Director of Transportation shall establish a small city advisory committee. The small
38 city advisory committee shall review department recommendations and approve applications sub-
39 mitted by small cities to the director. In consultation with the League of Oregon Cities, the director
40 shall appoint to the small city advisory committee one representative of a small city in each of the
41 five regions of this state.
42 (4) For purposes of this section:
43 (a) Region one consists of Clackamas, Hood River, Multnomah and Washington Counties.
44 (b) Region two consists of Benton, Clatsop, Columbia, Lane, Lincoln, Linn, Marion, Polk,
45 Tillamook and Yamhill Counties.
[16]

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 (c) Region three consists of Coos, Curry, Douglas, Jackson and Josephine Counties.
2 (d) Region four consists of Crook, Deschutes, Gilliam, Jefferson, Klamath, Lake, Sherman, Wasco
3 and Wheeler Counties.
4 (e) Region five consists of Baker, Grant, Harney, Malheur, Morrow, Umatilla, Union and
5 Wallowa Counties.

10 TRANSIT

12 SECTION 24. ORS 320.550 is amended to read:
13 320.550. (1) As used in this section:
14 (a) “Employer” has the meaning given that term in ORS 316.162.
15 (b) “Resident of this state” has the meaning given that term in ORS 316.027.
16 (c) “Wages” has the meaning given that term in ORS 316.162.
17 (2) A tax is imposed at the rate of [one-tenth] two-tenths of one percent of the wages of an
18 employee who is:
19 (a) A resident of this state, regardless of where services are performed.
20 (b) Not a resident of this state, for services performed in this state.
21 (3) Every employer at the time of the payment of wages shall deduct and withhold from the total
22 amount of the wages paid for services described under subsection (2) of this section an amount equal
23 to the total amount of wages multiplied by the rate of tax imposed under subsection (2) of this sec-
24 tion.
25 (4) An employer shall report and pay the tax imposed under this section to the Department of
26 Revenue at the time and in the manner determined by the department by rule.
27 (5) For purposes of the tax imposed under this section, an employer is considered a taxpayer.
28 (6) If a lender, surety or other person who supplies funds to or for the account of an employer
29 for the purpose of paying wages of the employees of such employer has actual notice or knowledge
30 that such employer does not intend to or will not be able to make timely payment or deposit of the
31 tax required to be deducted and withheld, such lender, surety or other person shall be liable to the
32 State of Oregon in a sum equal to the taxes, together with interest, that are not timely paid over
33 to the Department of Revenue. Such liability shall be limited to the principal amount supplied by
34 the lender, surety or other person, and any amounts so paid to the department shall be credited
35 against the liability of the employer.
36 (7)(a) An employer shall submit an annual return pursuant to ORS 316.202 to the Department
37 of Revenue. The amounts deducted from the wages during any calendar year in accordance with this
38 section shall be considered to be in payment of the tax imposed under subsection (2) of this section.
39 (b) The return submitted by the employer shall be accepted by the Department of Revenue as
40 evidence in favor of the employee of the amounts so deducted from the employee’s wages.
41 (8) Nothing in this section prohibits the Department of Revenue from including the tax imposed
42 under this section in the combined quarterly tax report required under ORS 316.168.
43 (9) An employer that fails to deduct and withhold the tax required under this section:
44 (a) Is deemed responsible for the payment of the tax obligation in an amount equal to the
45 amount required to be withheld from the employee’s wages and remitted to the Department of Re-
[17]

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 venue; and
2 (b) Is subject to a penalty of $250 per employee, up to a maximum penalty of $25,000, if the
3 employer knowingly fails to deduct and withhold the tax.
4 (10) Residents subject to the tax imposed under this section on wages earned outside this state
5 from an employer not doing business within this state shall report and pay the tax in an amount
6 not to exceed [one-tenth] two-tenths of one percent of the wages earned outside this state, and at
7 the time and in the manner, as determined by the Department of Revenue by rule.

40 under paragraph (a) of this subsection, a registered owner or lessee may elect to pay a flat
41 annual fee of $340.
42 (3) A subject vehicle is not subject to the additional amount of registration fees imposed
43 under ORS 803.422.

24 the fee applicable to the registered vehicle under ORS 803.422. For vehicles on which a flat fee is
25 imposed under ORS 803.420, the fee must be a whole dollar amount.
26 (b) A subject vehicle exempt under ORS 319.885 from the fees imposed under ORS 803.422
27 shall remain liable for any amount of vehicle registration fee imposed by a county under this
28 section that would be required if the exemption did not exist. As used in this subsection,
29 “subject vehicle” has the meaning given that term in ORS 319.883.
30 (5) Moneys from registration fees established under this section must be paid to the county es-
31 tablishing the registration fees as provided in ORS 802.110.
32 (6) Except as provided in ORS 801.044, or unless a different distribution is agreed upon by the
33 county and the cities within the jurisdiction of the county, the county ordinance shall provide for
34 payment of at least 40 percent of the moneys from registration fees established under this section
35 to cities within the county.
36 (7) The moneys for the cities and the county shall be used for any purpose for which moneys
37 from registration fees may be used, including the payment of debt service and costs related to bonds
38 or other obligations issued for such purposes.
39 (8) Two or more counties may act jointly to impose a registration fee under this section. The
40 ordinance of each county acting jointly with another under this subsection must provide for the
41 distribution of moneys collected through a joint registration fee.

31 (2) As a part of the project scoping phase, the Department of Transportation shall prepare a
32 written analysis of the costs and benefits of a transportation project. The analysis must state:
33 (a) The scope of the project;
34 (b) The period of analysis;
35 (c) The discount rate used in the analysis;
36 (d) The estimated costs to the department to undertake the project, including any costs for de-
37 sign, purchasing highway right-of-way and construction;
38 (e) The future costs to the department to preserve and maintain the project, discounted to
39 present value;
40 (f) Any other costs to the department;
41 (g) The costs to highway users that are associated with the project, including loss of safety,
42 delays in the time of travel and additional expenses for operating vehicles;
43 (h) The costs of any environmental impacts, including vehicle emissions and noise; and
44 (i) The value of the benefits of the project, including the value of any:
45 (A) Savings in the time of travel;
[28]

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 (B) Improvements to safety;
2 (C) Savings in the cost of operating vehicles; and

6 formance of routine maintenance scheduled by the department;

13 SECTION 64. Sections 65 to 67 of this 2025 special session Act are added to and made a
14 part of the Oregon Vehicle Code.
15 SECTION 65. “Dyed diesel” has the meaning given that term in ORS 319.520.
16 SECTION 66. (1) A person commits the offense of failure to comply with an international
17 fuel tax agreement if the person is required to comply with the requirements of an interna-
18 tional fuel tax agreement entered into under ORS 825.555 or any rule adopted by the De-
19 partment of Transportation under ORS 825.555, and the person fails to comply.
20 (2) The offense described under this section, failure to comply with an international fuel
21 tax agreement, is a Class A traffic violation.
22 SECTION 67. (1) A person commits the offense of improper use of dyed diesel if the
23 person operates a motor vehicle on the highways of this state and has dyed diesel in the fuel
24 supply tank of the vehicle in violation of section 71 of this 2025 special session Act.
25 (2) The offense described under this section, improper use of dyed diesel, is a Class A
26 traffic violation.

15 SECTION 70. Sections 71 and 72 of this 2025 special session Act are added to and made
16 a part of ORS 319.510 to 319.880.
17 SECTION 71. Dyed diesel use. (1) A person may operate or maintain a motor vehicle on
18 the highways of this state with dyed diesel in the fuel supply tank only if the use is author-
19 ized by an agency of the United States or the person is eligible for a refund under ORS
20 267.570 (2) or 319.831.
21 (2) A person that owns, operates or maintains a fuel storage tank or terminal storage
22 facility:
23 (a) Shall provide markings consistent with those directed by federal law; and
24 (b) May not knowingly store, or cause to be stored, dyed diesel in a fuel storage tank or
25 terminal storage facility if the purpose of the tank or facility is to store undyed diesel.
26 (3) A person that violates this section is subject to a civil penalty under section 72 of this
27 2025 special session Act.
28 SECTION 72. Civil penalties. (1) In addition to any other penalty provided by law, the
29 Department of Transportation may impose a civil penalty for failure to comply with section
30 71 of this 2025 special session Act.
31 (2) Any civil penalty imposed under this section shall be imposed in the manner provided
32 by ORS 183.745.
33 (3) The department shall adopt rules implementing these provisions, including a schedule
34 of civil penalties.
35 (4) The civil penalty for each violation of section 71 of this 2025 special session Act may
36 not exceed the amount of $10 per gallon of capacity of the fuel supply tank of the motor ve-
37 hicle, or $1,000, whichever is greater, plus the amount of tax that would have been paid for
38 an equivalent amount of motor vehicle fuel.
39 (5) A civil penalty imposed under this section may be remitted or reduced upon such
40 terms and conditions as the department considers proper and consistent with the public
41 health and safety.
42 (6)(a) In imposing a penalty pursuant to the schedule adopted pursuant to this section,
43 the department shall consider the following factors:
44 (A) Any prior violations of section 71 of this 2025 special session Act.
45 (B) The extent to which the violation threatens the public health or safety and the
[40]

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 immediacy of the threat.
2 (b) The penalty imposed under this section may be remitted or mitigated upon such
3 terms and conditions as the department determines to be proper and consistent with the
4 public benefit.
5 (7) All penalties recovered under this section shall be paid into the State Treasury and
6 credited to the State Highway Fund.

39 state in the transportation of persons or property, except vehicles operating wholly on fixed rails
40 or tracks and electric trolley buses. “Motor vehicle” includes overdimension vehicles or vehicles
41 permitted excessive weights pursuant to a special authorization issued by a city, county or the De-
42 partment of Transportation.
43 [(10)] (11) “Permit” means an authority issued to a carrier under ORS 825.102, 825.104, 825.106,
44 825.108 or 825.127.
45 [(11)] (12) “Private carrier” means any person who operates a motor vehicle over the public
[43]

A-Eng. HB 3991
1 highways of this state for the purpose of transporting persons or property when the transportation
2 is incidental to a primary business enterprise, other than transportation, in which such person is
3 engaged.
4 [(12)] (13) “Privilege taxes” means the weight-mile tax and fees prescribed in this chapter.
5 [(13)] (14) “Property” includes, but is not limited to, permanent loads such as equipment, appli-
6 ances, devices, or ballast that are attached to, carried on, or made a part of the vehicle and that
7 are designed to serve some functional purpose.
8 [(14)] (15) “Public highway” means every street, alley, road, highway and thoroughfare in this
9 state used by the public or dedicated or appropriated to public use.
10 [(15)] (16) “Transit-type motor vehicle” means any passenger-carrying vehicle that does not have
11 a separate space for transporting baggage or express.
12 [(16)] (17) “Transporter” has the meaning given that term in ORS 466.005.
13 SECTION 79. Section 80 of this 2025 special session Act is added to and made a part of
14 ORS chapter 825.
15 SECTION 80. (1) Before operating a motor vehicle on the public highways of this state,
16 an out-of-state motor carrier not licensed under an international fuel tax agreement shall
17 obtain a valid fuel trip permit from the Department of Transportation in accordance with
18 this section. A motor carrier shall obtain a fuel trip permit under this section if:
19 (a) The motor carrier is operating a motor vehicle that is not a recreational vehicle:
20 (A) Having two axles and a gross vehicle weight or registered gross vehicle weight ex-
21 ceeding 26,000 pounds;
22 (B) Having three or more axles regardless of weight; or
23 (C) Used in combination, when the weight of such combination exceeds 26,000 pounds; and
24 (b) The vehicle is not registered under ORS 826.009 or 826.031.
25 (2) Subsection (1) of this section does not apply to a motor carrier that has a valid
26 international fuel tax agreement license issued by a jurisdiction other than Oregon.
27 (3) The Department of Transportation shall develop a standardized application form for
28 a fuel trip permit issued under this section.
29 (4) The department may not issue more than three fuel trip permits in a calendar year
30 for any one motor vehicle.
31 (5) No report of mileage is required for the motor vehicle to which the fuel trip permit
32 relates.
33 (6) A fuel trip permit issued under this section is valid:
34 (a) For three consecutive days beginning and ending on the dates specified on the face
35 of the fuel trip permit; and
36 (b) Only for the motor vehicle for which the fuel trip permit was issued.
37 (7) The fee for the fuel trip permit shall be determined by the department by rule.
38 (8) The department may adopt rules to carry out the provisions of this section.

20 such operation computed at the following rate for each 100 pounds of declared combined
21 weight:
22 (A) For electric motor vehicles, $10.94.
23 (B) For vehicles other than electric motor vehicles, $7.57.
24 (b) Any carrier electing to pay fees under this method may, as to vehicles otherwise exempt from
25 taxation, elect to be taxed on the mileage basis for movements of such empty vehicles over public
26 highways whenever operations are for the purpose of repair, maintenance, servicing or moving from
27 one exempt highway operation to another.
28 (2) The annual fees provided in subsections (1) and (3) of this section may be paid on a monthly
29 basis. Any carrier electing to pay fees under this method may not change an election during the
30 same calendar year in which the election is made, but may be relieved from the payment due for
31 any month during which a motor vehicle is not operated. A carrier electing to pay fees under this
32 method shall report and pay these fees on or before the 10th of each month for the preceding
33 month’s operations. A monthly report shall be made on all vehicles on the annual fee basis including
34 any vehicle not operated for the month.
35 [(3)(a)] (3) In lieu of other fees provided in ORS 825.474, carriers engaged in the operation of
36 motor vehicles equipped with dump bodies and used in the transportation of sand, gravel, rock, dirt,
37 debris, cinders, asphaltic concrete mix, metallic ores and concentrates or raw nonmetallic products,
38 whether crushed or otherwise, moving from mines, pits or quarries may pay annual fees for such
39 operation computed at the following rate [of $16.98] for each 100 pounds of declared combined
40 weight[.]:
41 (a) For electric motor vehicles, $17.69.
42 (b) For vehicles other than electric motor vehicles, $12.25.
43 [(b) Any carrier electing to pay fees under this method may, as to vehicles otherwise exempt for
44 taxation, elect to be taxed on the mileage basis for movements of such empty vehicles over public
45 highways whenever operations are for the purpose of repair, maintenance, servicing or moving from
[53]

1 one exempt highway operation to another.]
2 SECTION 98. ORS 818.225 is amended to read:
3 818.225. (1) As used in this section, “equivalent single-axle load” means the relationship between
4 actual or requested weight and an 18,000 pound single-axle load as determined by the American
5 Association of State Highway and Transportation Officials Road Tests reported at the Proceedings
6 Conference of 1962.
7 (2)(a) In addition to any fee for a single-trip nondivisible load permit, a person who is issued the
8 permit or who operates a vehicle in a manner that requires the permit is liable for payment of a
9 road use assessment fee of [ten and nine-tenths] seven and nine-tenths cents per equivalent
10 single-axle load mile traveled.
11 (b) If the road use assessment fee is not collected at the time of issuance of the permit, the de-
12 partment shall bill the permittee for the amount due. The account shall be considered delinquent if
13 not paid within 60 days of billing.
14 (c) The miles of travel authorized by a single-trip nondivisible load permit shall be exempt from
15 taxation under ORS chapter 825.
16 (3) The department may adopt rules:
17 (a) To standardize the determination of equivalent single-axle load computation based on aver-
18 age highway conditions; and
19 (b) To establish procedures for payment, collection and enforcement of the fees and assessments
20 established by this chapter.
21 SECTION 99. (1) The amendments to ORS 825.474, 825.476 and 825.480 by sections 92, 94
22 and 96 of this 2025 special session Act become operative on July 1, 2027.
23 (2) The amendments to ORS 818.225, 825.474, 825.476 and 825.480 by sections 93, 95, 97 and
24 98 of this 2025 special session Act become operative on July 1, 2029.
25 SECTION 100. (1) The amendments to ORS 825.474, 825.476 and 825.480 by sections 92, 94
26 and 96 of this 2025 special session Act apply to taxes imposed on or after July 1, 2027.
27 (2) The amendments to ORS 818.225, 825.474, 825.476 and 825.480 by sections 93, 95, 97 and
28 98 of this 2025 special session Act apply to taxes imposed on or after July 1, 2029.
